## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials constitutive modeling (thermo-mechanical stress–strain)
**Analysis**: The variables match a thermo-mechanical constitutive law where stress sigma depends on strain epsilon and temperature T through elastic modulus changes, thermal expansion (strain offset), and temperature-dependent yielding/strain hardening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelasticity (thermal strain offset): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * (T - c3)) (elastic response with temperature-dependent modulus and thermal expansion)
- Hooke’s law with modulus softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (small-strain elasticity with E(T))
- Temperature-dependent yield stress (piecewise elastic-perfectly plastic, smooth approx): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon - c2 * log(1 + exp(c3 * ((c4 + c5 * T) * epsilon - (c6 + c7 * T)))) (elastic then capped/regularized by yield)
- Ludwik/Hollomon hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 + c3 * T) * (epsilon + c4)**c5 (plastic hardening with temperature-dependent strength)
- Ramberg–Osgood (implicit form rearranged): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (nonlinear elastic/plastic transition; solve for sigma given epsilon,T)
- Voce saturation hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 + c3 * T) * (1 - exp(-(c4 + c5 * T) * epsilon)) (hardening approaching saturation, temperature shifts saturation rate/level)
- Exponential thermal softening of flow stress: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) * exp(-(c3 + c4 * epsilon) * T) (stress decreases with temperature; strain changes sensitivity)
- Johnson–Cook-like (strain hardening × thermal softening; no rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - (c3 * T)**c4) (empirical plasticity with multiplicative temperature softening)
- Hyperelastic 1D neo-Hookean-type with temperature-dependent shear modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * ((1 + epsilon) - (1 + epsilon)**(-2)) (large-strain elastic response, modulus depends on T)
- Thermally activated barrier (Eyring-like) for flow stress: sigma = c0 + c1 * asinh((c2 * epsilon) * exp(c3 / (T + c4))) (plastic flow controlled by thermal activation; sigma decreases with increasing T)
- Combined elastic + viscoplastic-like saturation (phenomenological): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * tanh((c4 + c5 * T) * epsilon) (initial linear stiffness plus saturating inelastic contribution)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal expansion appears as a strain shift: sigma depends on (epsilon - c * (T - T0)) rather than epsilon alone (stress-free strain moves with temperature).
- Elastic modulus often decreases with T, so prefactors like (c0 + c1*T + c2*T**2) multiplying epsilon are common (E(T) softening/stiffening).
- Yield/flow stress typically decreases with T; multiplicative softening factors such as exp(-c*T) or (1 - (c*T)**m) encode thermal softening.
- Strain hardening is commonly concave-down with increasing epsilon; saturation forms 1 - exp(-c*epsilon) (Voce) capture approach to a limiting stress.
- Power-law hardening (epsilon + c)**n captures straight lines on log–log plots of stress vs strain and is widely used for plastic regimes.
- Smooth transition from elastic to plastic can be represented by adding a saturating nonlinearity (tanh, log(1+exp(.))) rather than a hard piecewise yield.
- Large-strain elasticity often depends on stretch lambda = 1 + epsilon with terms like lambda - lambda^(-2), reflecting incompressible hyperelastic response.
- Coupled sensitivity where temperature changes hardening rate (e.g., exp(-(c0+c1*T)*epsilon)) reflects dynamic recovery/recrystallization-like effects in phenomenological fits.
- Thermally activated flow can introduce inverse-temperature inside exponentials (exp(c/(T+c0))) combined with asinh/log, reflecting barrier-crossing kinetics in plasticity.
